<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'><b><u>PART I</u></b></p>

<h2><b>&nbsp;</b></h2>

<h2><b>Overview</b></h2>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>This Annual Report on
Form 10-K for the year ended December 31, 2005, includes the financial statements
of PDC 2005-A Limited Partnership (&quot;the Partnership&quot;) for the year ended
December 31, 2005 and substantially all
of the information for the quarters ended June 30, 2005 and September 30, 2005
that would normally be contained in Quarterly Reports on Form 10-Q.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>As
previously reported in an update included in Form 12b-25 (Notification of Late
Filing) filed with the SEC on March 31, 2006, the Managing General Partner had
suspended filing financial reports pending the complete assessment of its Partnership
oil and gas property accounting and to correct potential errors related to
depreciation, asset impairments, asset retirement obligations and hedge
accounting.&nbsp; As a result of this review of our accounting policies and
practices, we determined that the Partnership's previously filed financial
statements do not require restatement.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><b>&nbsp;</b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><b><u>ITEM 1.</u></b><b><u>&nbsp; BUSINESS</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><u>General</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>PDC
2005-A Limited Partnership was organized as a limited partnership pursuant to
the West Virginia Uniform Limited Partnership Act for the purpose of
aggregating funds for the exploration and production of oil and natural gas. Business operations of the Partnership commenced on February 9,
2005, upon the closing of the offering for the sale of partnership units.
</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Pursuant
to a registration statement filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission,
limited and general partnership interests were registered for an offering under
the PDC 2004-2006 Drilling Program for the formation of a series of limited
partnerships.&nbsp; PDC 2005-A Limited Partnership was formed with total
capital contributions of $39,937,470 from limited partners and additional
general partners (collectively, the &quot;Investor Partners&quot;) and $8,829,000 in
capital contributed by Petroleum Development Corporation (&quot;PDC&quot;), the Managing
General Partner. Total funding of the Partnership was $48,766,470.&nbsp; The
capital contributions from the Investor Partners consisted of 1,996.87
partnership units at a unit price of $20,000 each. After syndication costs of
$4,022,407 and a one time management fee to the Managing General Partner of
$599,062, the Partnership had available cash of $44,145,001 to commence
Partnership activities for the drilling of natural gas and oil wells. During
2006, all additional general partners were converted to limited partners under
provisions of the partnership agreement.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal>Under the terms of the
partnership agreement, the allocation of production revenues among the Investor
Partners and the Managing General Partner is as follows:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Operating
and direct costs are allocated and charged to the Investor Partners and the
Managing General Partner in the same percentages as revenues are
allocated.&nbsp; See &quot;Note 4 - Allocation of Partners' Interests&quot; in the Notes
to the Financial Statements for a complete description of the allocation of all
Partnership revenues and costs.</p>



<p class=toch2 style='margin-bottom:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'>Drilling
Activities</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Since
its formation, the Partnership has been engaged in onshore, domestic oil and
natural gas exploration and production exclusively in the Rocky Mountain
Region. The Partnership participated in the drilling of only development
wells.&nbsp; Due to natural gas being the predominant production, all wells are
classified as gas wells, although significant amounts of oil can be produced in
association with the gas. The following
table summarizes the Partnership's drilling activities during 2005 related to
its 49 wells:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>As
of December 31, 2005, completion of one well was delayed until the spring of
2006 due to weather conditions restricting access to the well site.&nbsp; As of
the filing of this report, all 49 wells have been completed.&nbsp; The 49 wells
in the table above are the only wells the Partnership will drill because all of
the capital contributions provided by the partnership offering will have been
utilized upon completion of the remaining well. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal>Additional information
concerning the Partnership's gas wells is contained in &quot;Item 2 - Properties&quot;
below.</p>



<p class=toch2 style='margin-bottom:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'>Plan of
Operations</p>



<p class=MsoBodyText>Under agreement with the Investor Partners, the Managing
General Partner serves as operator for the drilling of the Partnership's wells and
for the production and sale of natural gas and oil from the wells. Once producing, the Partnership's wells will be
produced until they are depleted or until they are uneconomical to
produce.&nbsp; PDC plans to recomplete the Codell formation in most of the wells in the Wattenberg
Field after five or more years of production because these wells will usually
have experienced a significant decline in production in that time period.&nbsp;
These Codell recompletions
typically increase the production rates and recoverable reserves.&nbsp; Prior
experience of PDC and other producers with Codell recompletions has resulted in significant production
increases for most wells, although not all recompletions
have been successful. The cost of a Codell recompletion is about one-third of the cost of a new well
(currently about $180,000).&nbsp; The Managing General Partner will arrange for
contractors to perform the work, the cost of which will be paid out of overall
revenues of the Partnership.&nbsp; PDC will pay its proportionate share of
costs based on the operating costs sharing ratios of the Partnership.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Employees</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership has no employees. Services to the Partnership are provided by PDC,
which has a total of approximately 170 employees, including personnel in
accounting and finance, administration, engineering, geology, field operations,
and natural gas marketing. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Markets for Oil and Gas</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
availability of a market for any oil and natural gas produced from the
operation of the Partnership's wells will depend upon a number of factors
beyond the control of the Partnership which cannot be accurately
predicted.&nbsp; These factors include the proximity of the Partnership wells
to and the capacity of natural gas pipelines, the availability and price of
competitive fuels, fluctuations in seasonal supply and demand, and government
regulation of supply and demand created by its pricing and allocation
restrictions.&nbsp; Oversupplies of gas can be expected to occur from time to
time and may result in the Partnership's wells being shut-in or production
being curtailed.&nbsp; Increased imports of oil and natural gas have occurred
and are expected to continue. The effects of such imports could adversely
impact the market for domestic oil and natural gas. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>PDC
utilizes the services of its wholly-owned subsidiary, Riley Natural Gas (RNG),
in marketing the oil and natural gas produced from Partnership wells.&nbsp; RNG
has been in the gas marketing business since 1986. All oil and natural gas is
sold under contracts based on market sensitive indexes that vary from month to
month. No fixed price contracts are in place. &nbsp;Purchase contracts for the
sale of oil are cancelable on 30 days notice, whereas purchase contracts for
the sale of natural gas may range from spot market sales of short duration to
contracts with a term of a number of years and that may require the dedication
of the gas from a well for a period ranging up to the life of the well.&nbsp;
PDC will not make any commitment of future production that does not primarily
benefit the Partnership.&nbsp; RNG is entitled to charge reasonable fees for
its services, including out-of-pocket costs, which will be equal to or less
than fees charged to non-affiliated producers for similar services. The
Partnership sold its oil and natural gas to three customers during 2005, which
accounted for 49%, 33% and 18% of the Partnership's total oil and natural gas
sales for the period.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>-5-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='page-break-before:always'>




<p class=MsoNormal><u>Derivatives and Hedging
Activities</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Historically,
PDC and RNG have utilized commodity based derivative instruments to manage a
portion of the exposure to price volatility stemming from natural gas and crude
oil production.&nbsp; In order to provide a more predictable cash flow stream,
PDC expects to continue the use of derivative instruments, including the
Partnership's production of natural gas and oil, and will enter into derivative
contracts on behalf of the Partnership.&nbsp; PDC may use financial hedges, put
options, call options, and other derivative instruments to offset variations in
prices.&nbsp; The contracts hedge committed and anticipated natural gas and oil
sales generally forecasted to occur within the next two-year period. The
Managing General Partner does not hold or issue derivatives for trading or
speculative purposes and permits utilization of hedges only if there is an
underlying physical position.&nbsp; See &quot;Commodity Price Risk&quot; under Item 7A
below.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><u>Competition</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>The Partnership competes in marketing its gas and oil
with numerous companies and individuals, many of which have financial resources,
staffs and facilities substantially greater than those of the Partnership or
PDC.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><u>Governmental Regulations</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>Federal and state regulatory authorities have
established rules and regulations requiring permits for well operations,
reclamation bonds and reports concerning operations.&nbsp; States also have
statutes and regulations concerning the spacing of wells, environmental matters
and conservation, and have established regulations concerning the unitization
and pooling of oil and gas properties and maximum rates of production from oil
and gas wells. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u>Natural Gas Regulation</u>.&nbsp;
Sale of natural gas by the Partnership is subject to regulation of production,
transportation and pricing by governmental regulatory agencies.&nbsp;
Generally, the regulatory agency in the state where a producing well is located
regulates production activities and, in addition, the transportation of gas
sold intrastate.&nbsp; The Federal Energy Regulatory Commission (FERC)
regulates the operation and cost of interstate pipeline operators who transport
gas.&nbsp; Currently, the price of gas sold by the Partnership is not regulated
by any state or federal agency.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u>Environmental and Safety
Regulations</u>.&nbsp; The Partnership believes that it complies, in
all material respects, with all legislation and regulations relating to
environmental and safety matters in the drilling and production of oil and gas
wells and the discharge of wastes.&nbsp; Compliance with such provisions and
regulations is significant during well development but has not had a material
effect upon the Partnership's expenditures for capital equipment, its
operations or its competitive position.&nbsp; The cost of such compliance is
not anticipated to be material in the future.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership believes it has complied in all material respects with applicable
state and federal regulations. The Partnership estimates it has spent
approximately $580,000 in 2005 to comply with federal and state regulations,
primarily relating to environmental permitting and compliance.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM
1A.</u></b><b><u>&nbsp; RISK
FACTORS </u></b></p>



<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify;text-indent:0in'>In the course of its normal
business, the Partnership is subject to a number of risks that could adversely
impact its business, operating results, financial condition, and cash
distributions.&nbsp; The following risk factors should be considered carefully
in addition to the other information included in this report.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Drilling natural gas and oil wells is
speculative and may be unprofitable or result in the total loss of investment. The drilling and completion
operations undertaken by the Partnership for the development of natural gas and
oil reserves are inherently speculative and involve a high degree of risk and
the possibility of a total loss of investment.&nbsp; Drilling activities may
result in unprofitable well operations, not only from non-productive wells, but
also from wells that do not produce natural gas or oil in sufficient quantities
or quality to return a profit on the amounts expended.&nbsp; Consequently,
Partnership wells may not produce sufficient natural gas and oil for investors
to receive a profit or even to recover their initial investment.&nbsp; Only one
of the prior Partnerships sponsored by PDC has, to date, generated cash
distributions in excess of investor subscriptions without tax savings.&nbsp;
PDC cannot predict whether any prospect will produce commercial quantities of
natural gas or oil.&nbsp; PDC cannot predict the life and the ultimate
production of any well, and the actual lives could differ from those
anticipated.</p>

<p class=toch3 align=center style='text-align:center'>-6-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>The partnership units are not
registered, there will be no public market for the units, and as a result, an
Investor Partner may not be able to sell his or her units.&nbsp; There is and will be
no public market for the units nor will a public market develop for the
units.&nbsp; Investor Partners may not be able to sell their Partnership
interests or may be able to sell them only for less than fair market
value.&nbsp; The offer and sale of units have not been, and will not in the
future, be registered under the Securities Act or under any state securities
laws.&nbsp; Each purchaser of units has been required to represent that such
investor has purchased the units for his or her own account for investment and
not with a view to resale or distribution.&nbsp; No transfer of a unit may be
made unless the transferee is a &quot;qualified investor&quot; and such
transfer is registered under the Securities Act and applicable state securities
laws, or an exemption therefrom is available.&nbsp;
The Partnership may require that the transferor provide an opinion of legal
counsel stating that the transfer complies with all applicable securities
laws.&nbsp; A sale or transfer of units by an investor requires PDC's prior written consent.&nbsp; For these and other
reasons, an investor must anticipate that he or she will have to hold his or
her Partnership interests indefinitely and will not be able to liquidate his or
her investment in the Partnership.&nbsp; Consequently, an investor must be able
to bear the economic risk of investing in the Partnership for an indefinite
period of time.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>The additional general partners will
be individually liable for Partnership obligations and liabilities that arose
prior to conversion to limited partners (which can occur only after the
drilling completion operations are finished) that are beyond the amount of
their subscriptions, partnership assets, and the assets of the Managing General
Partner.&nbsp; Under
West Virginia law, the state in which the Partnership has organized, general
partners of a limited partnership have unlimited liability with respect to the
partnership.&nbsp; Therefore, the additional general partners of the
Partnership will be liable individually and as a group for all obligations and
liabilities of creditors and claimants, whether arising out of contract or tort
or in the conduct of the Partnership's operations, until such time as the additional
general partners are converted to limited partners.&nbsp; Under the Partnership
Agreement, this conversion is not scheduled to occur until the drilling and
completion operations are finished.&nbsp; Irrespective of conversion, the
additional general partners will remain fully liable for obligations and
liabilities that arose prior to conversion.&nbsp; Investors as additional
general partners may be liable for amounts in excess of their subscriptions,
the assets of the Partnership, including insurance coverage, and the assets of
the Managing General Partner.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>The Partnership may retain
Partnership revenues if needed for Partnership operations to fully develop the
Partnership's wells; if full development of the Partnership's wells proves
commercially unsuccessful, an investor might anticipate a reduction in cash
distributions.&nbsp; The
Partnership intends to utilize substantially all available capital raised in the offering for the drilling and completion of
wells and will have only nominal funds available for Partnership purposes prior
to the time of production from Partnership well operations.&nbsp; In the
future, PDC may wish to rework or recomplete
Partnership wells but PDC has not held money from the initial investment for
that future work.&nbsp; There is no assurance that future development of the
Partnership's wells will prove commercially successful and that the
further-developed Partnership wells will generate sufficient funds from
production to increase distributions to the investors to cover revenues
retained.&nbsp; If future development of the Partnership's wells is not
commercially successful, the use of funds retained from production revenues
could result in a reduction of cash distributions to the Investor Partners. </p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Increases in prices of oil and
natural gas have increased the cost of drilling and development and may affect
the performance of the Partnership in both the short and long term.&nbsp; In the current high
price environment, most oil and gas companies have increased their expenditures
for drilling new wells.&nbsp; This has resulted in increased demand and higher
cost for leases, oilfield services and well equipment.&nbsp; Because of these
higher costs, the risk to the Partnership of decreased profitability from
future decreases in oil and natural gas prices is increased.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Reductions in prices of oil and
natural gas reduce the profitability of the Partnership's production
operations.&nbsp; Global
economic conditions, political conditions, and energy conservation have created
unstable prices.&nbsp; Revenues of the Partnership are directly related to
natural gas and oil prices for which PDC cannot predict.&nbsp; The prices for
domestic natural gas and oil production have varied substantially over time and
by location, and are likely to remain extremely unstable.&nbsp; Revenue from the sale of oil and natural gas increases when prices
for these commodities increase and declines when prices decrease.&nbsp;
These unpredictable price changes can occur rapidly and are not within the
control of the Partnership.&nbsp; A decline in natural gas and/or oil prices
would result in lower revenues for the Partnership and a reduction of cash
distributions to the partners of the Partnership.</p>

<p class=toch3 align=center style='text-align:center'>-7-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>The high level of drilling activity
could result in an oversupply of natural gas on a regional or national level,
resulting in much lower commodity prices.&nbsp; Recently, the natural gas market has been
characterized by excess demand compared to the supplies available, leading in
general to higher prices for natural gas.&nbsp; The high level of drilling,
combined with a reduction in demand resulting from higher prices, could result
in an oversupply of natural gas.&nbsp; In the Rocky Mountain region, rapid
growth of production and increasing supplies may result in lower prices and
production curtailment due to limitations on available pipeline facilities or markets
not developed to utilize or transport the new supplies.&nbsp; In both cases,
the result would probably be lower prices for the natural gas the Partnership produces, reduced profitability for the Partnership and
reduced cash distributions to the Investor Partners.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Sufficient insurance coverage may not
be available for the Partnership, thereby increasing the risk of loss for the
Investor Partners.&nbsp;
It is possible that some or all of the insurance coverage which the Partnership
has available may become unavailable or prohibitively expensive.&nbsp; In that
case, PDC might elect to change the insurance coverage.&nbsp; The additional
general partners could be exposed to additional financial risk due to the
reduced insurance coverage and due to the fact that additional general partners
would continue to be individually liable for obligations and liabilities of the
Partnership.&nbsp; Investor Partners could be subject to greater risk of loss
of their investment because less insurance would be available to protect the
Partnership from casualty losses.&nbsp; Moreover, should the Partnership's cost
of insurance become more expensive, the amount of cash distributions to the
investors will be reduced.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'>Through
their involvement in Partnership and other non-partnership activities, the
Managing General Partner and its affiliates have interests which conflict with
those of the Investor Partners; actions taken by the Managing General Partner
in furtherance of its own interests could result in the Partnership's being
less profitable and a reduction in cash distributions to the investors.&nbsp; PDC's
continued active participation in oil and natural gas activities for its own
account and on behalf of other partnerships organized or to be organized by PDC
and the manner in which Partnership revenues are allocated create conflicts of
interest with the Partnership.&nbsp; PDC has interests which inherently
conflict with the interests of the investor partners.&nbsp; In operating the
Partnership, the Managing General Partner and its affiliates could take actions
which benefit themselves and which do not benefit the Partnership.&nbsp; These
actions could result in the Partnership's being less profitable.&nbsp; In that
event, an Investor Partner could anticipate a reduction of cash distributions.</p>



<p class=toch3 style='margin-top:0in;text-align:justify'>The Partnership and
other partnerships sponsored by the Managing General Partner may compete with
each other for prospects, equipment, contractors, and personnel; as a result,
the Partnership may find it more difficult to operate effectively and
profitably.&nbsp; During
and after 2006, PDC plans to offer interests in other partnerships to be formed
for substantially the same purposes as those of the Partnership.&nbsp;
Therefore, a number of partnerships with unexpended capital funds, including
those partnerships formed before and after the Partnership, may exist at the
same time.&nbsp; The Partnership may compete for equipment, contractors, and
PDC personnel (when the Partnership is also needful of equipment, contractors
and PDC personnel), which may make it more difficult and more costly to obtain
services for the Partnership.&nbsp; In that event, it is possible that the
Partnership would be less profitable.&nbsp; Additionally, because PDC must
divide its attention in the management of its own affairs as well as the
affairs of the 74 other limited partnerships PDC has organized, the Partnership
will not receive PDC's full attention and efforts at
all times.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>The Partnership's derivative
activities could result in reduced revenue compared to the level the
Partnership might experience if no derivative instruments were in place.&nbsp; The Partnership expects
to use derivative instruments to reduce the impact of price movements on
revenue.&nbsp; While these derivative instruments protect the Partnership
against the impact of declining prices, they also may limit the positive impact
of price increases.&nbsp; As a result, the Partnership may have lower revenues
when prices are increasing than might otherwise be the case, and may also
reduce the Partnership's cash flows and cash distributions to the Investor
Partners.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Hedging transactions have in the past
and may in the future impact our cash flow from operations.&nbsp; Our commodity
hedging may prevent us from benefiting fully from price increases and may
expose us to other risks.&nbsp;
PDC will enter into hedging arrangements to reduce the Partnership's exposure
to fluctuations in natural gas and crude oil prices and to achieve more
predictable cash flow.&nbsp; Although the Partnership's hedging activities may
limit the Partnership's exposure to declines in natural gas and crude oil
prices, these activities may also limit and have in the past limited,
additional revenues from increases in natural gas and crude oil prices.&nbsp;
To the extent that the Partnership engages in hedging activities to protect
itself from commodity price volatility, the Partnership may be prevented from
realizing the benefits of price increases above the levels of the hedges.&nbsp;
</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=toch3 align=center style='text-align:center'>-8-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='page-break-before:always'>


<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Additionally, the hedging transactions PDC has entered
into, or will enter into, may not adequately protect the Partnership from
financial loss due to circumstances such as:</p>

<p class=toch3 style='margin-top:6.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:6.0pt;
margin-left:74.9pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Highly volatile natural gas and
crude oil prices;</p>

<p class=toch3 style='margin-top:6.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:6.0pt;
margin-left:74.9pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Production being
less than expected; or</p>

<p class=toch3 style='margin-left:74.9pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
A counterparty defaults on its
contractual obligations.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'>A significant
financial loss by the Managing General Partner could result in PDC's inability to indemnify additional general partners
for personal losses suffered because of Partnership liabilities.&nbsp; As a result of PDC's commitments as Managing General Partner of several
partnerships and because of the unlimited liability of a general partner to
third parties, PDC's net worth is at risk of
reduction if PDC suffers a significant financial loss.&nbsp; Because PDC is
primarily responsible for the conduct of the Partnership's affairs as well as
the affairs of other partnerships for which PDC serves as managing general
partner, a significant adverse financial reversal for PDC could result in PDC's inability to pay for Partnership liabilities and
obligations.&nbsp; The additional general partners of the Partnership might be
personally liable for payments of the Partnership's liabilities and
obligations.&nbsp; Therefore, the Managing General Partner's financial
incapacity could increase the risk of personal liability as an additional
general partner because PDC would be unable to indemnify the additional general
partners for any personal losses they suffered arising from Partnership
operations.</p>



<p class=dmbodytext5 style='text-align:justify'><u>The Managing General Partner
may not have sufficient funds or budget to repurchase limited partnership
units.</u>&nbsp; As a result of the Managing General Partner being a general
partner in several partnerships, the Partnership's net worth is at risk of
reduction if PDC suffers a significant financial loss.&nbsp; Because the
investors may request the Managing General Partner to repurchase the units in
the Partnership, subject to certain conditions and restrictions, a significant
adverse financial reversal could result in the Managing General Partner's
inability to pay for Partnership obligations or the repurchase of investor
units.&nbsp; </p>

<p class=dmbodytext5 style='text-align:justify'><u>Fluctuating market
conditions and government regulations may cause a decline in the profitability
of the Partnership.</u>&nbsp; The sale of any natural gas and oil produced by
the Partnership will be affected by fluctuating market conditions and
governmental regulations, including environmental and safety standards set by
state and federal agencies.&nbsp; From time-to-time, a surplus of natural gas
or oil may occur in areas of the United States.&nbsp; The effect of a surplus
may be to reduce the price the Partnership receives for the natural gas or oil
production, or to reduce the amount of natural gas or oil that the Partnership
may produce and sell.&nbsp; As a result, the Partnership may not be
profitable.&nbsp; Lower prices and/or lower production and sales will result in
lower revenues for the Partnership and a reduction in cash distributions to the
partners of the Partnership.</p>

<p class=toch3 style='text-align:justify'>Environmental hazards involved in
drilling natural gas and oil wells may result in substantial liabilities for
the Partnership.&nbsp;
There are numerous natural hazards involved in the drilling of wells, including
unexpected or unusual formations, pressures, blowouts involving possible
damages to property and third parties, surface damages, personal injury or loss
of life, damage to and loss of equipment, reservoir damage and loss of
reserves.&nbsp; Uninsured liabilities would reduce the funds available to the
Partnership, may result in the loss of Partnership properties, and may create
liability for additional general partners.&nbsp; The Partnership may become
subject to liability for pollution, abuses of the environment and other similar
damages and insurance coverage may be insufficient to protect the Partnership
against all potential losses.&nbsp; In that event, Partnership assets would be
used to pay personal injury and property damage claims and the costs of
controlling blowouts or replacing destroyed equipment rather than for drilling
activities.&nbsp; These payments would cause an otherwise profitable
partnership to be less profitable or unprofitable and would result in a
reduction of cash distributions to the partners of the Partnership.</p>

<p style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u>Information
concerning our reserves and future net revenues estimates is inherently
uncertain.</u>&nbsp; The accuracy of proved reserves estimates and
estimated future net revenues from such reserves is a function of the quality
of available geological, geophysical, engineering and economic data and is
subject to various assumptions, including assumptions required by the SEC
relating to oil and gas prices, drilling and operating expenses, and other
matters. Although we believe that our estimated proved reserves represent
reserves that we are reasonably certain to recover, actual future production,
oil and gas prices, revenues, taxes, development expenditures, operating expenses
and quantities of recoverable oil and gas reserves will most likely vary from
the assumptions and estimates used to determine proved reserves. Any
significant variance could materially affect the estimated quantities and value
of our oil and gas reserves, which in turn could adversely affect our cash
flow, results of operations and the availability of capital resources. In
addition, we may adjust estimates of proved reserves to reflect production
history, results of exploration and development, prevailing oil and gas prices
and other factors, many of which are beyond our control. Downward adjustments
to our estimated proved reserves could require us to write down the carrying
value of our oil and gas properties, which would reduce our earnings and our
partners' equity.</p>

<p align=center style='text-align:center;text-indent:.5in'>-9-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'>The
present value of proved reserves will not necessarily equal the current fair
market value of our estimated oil and gas reserves. In accordance with the
reserve reporting requirements of the SEC, the estimated discounted future net cash flows from proved reserves are
based on prices and costs as of the date of the estimate. Actual future prices
and costs may be materially higher or lower than those as of the date of the
estimate. The timing of both the production and the expenses with respect to
the development and production of oil and gas properties will affect the timing
of future net cash flows from proved reserves and their present value.</p>

<p style='text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u>Seasonal
weather conditions may adversely affect the Partnership's ability to conduct
drilling, completion and production activities in some of the areas where we
operate.</u>&nbsp; Oil and natural gas
operations in the Rocky Mountains are adversely affected by seasonal weather
conditions. In certain areas, drilling and other oil and natural gas activities
are restricted or prevented by weather conditions for up to 6 months out of the
year. This limits operations in those areas and can intensify competition
during those months for drilling rigs, oil field equipment, services, supplies
and qualified personnel, which may lead to periodic shortages. These
constraints and the resulting shortages or high costs could delay operations
and materially increase operating and capital costs and therefore, adversely
affect profitability. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM
1B.</u></b><b><u>&nbsp; UNRESOLVED
STAFF COMMENTS</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal>None.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM
2.</u></b><b><u>&nbsp; PROPERTIES</u></b></p>



<p class=document1 style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:auto'>The Partnership's properties consist of
oil and gas wells, associated well equipment, and the ownership in leasehold
acreage assigned to the spacing units on which the 49 wells were drilled.&nbsp;
The Partnership has no undeveloped acreage.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Drilling Activity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><br>
The Partnership commenced drilling activities on March 5, 2005, following
funding of the Partnership, and as of December 31, 2005, all wells had been
completed except for one well that was in progress at year end.&nbsp; All of
the Partnership's wells are located in Colorado. The following table sets forth
the results of the Partnership's drilling activity as of December 31,
2005.&nbsp; </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>As
of the date of this report, all 49 of the total wells drilled by the
Partnership are considered productive wells.&nbsp; The Partnership did not
participate in the drilling of any exploratory wells. The one well in progress
at year end was drilled in late 2005, but the completion was delayed until the
spring of 2006 due to weather conditions restricting access to the well site.&nbsp;
The 49 wells in the table above are the only wells to be drilled by the
Partnership since all of the funds raised in the Partnership offering of
$44,145,001 will have been utilized upon the completion of the one remaining
well.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>A
development well is a well that is drilled close to and into the same formation
as wells which have already produced and sold oil or
natural gas.&nbsp; An exploratory well is one which is drilled in an area where
there has been no oil or natural gas production, or a well which is drilled to
a previously untested or non-producing zone in an area where there are wells
producing from other formations.&nbsp; Productive wells consist of producing
wells and wells capable of producing oil and gas in commercial quantities,
including gas wells awaiting pipeline connections to commence deliveries.&nbsp;
A gross well refers to the number of wells in which the Partnership has an
interest.&nbsp; A net well refers to a gross well multiplied by the percentage
working interest in the wells owned by the Partnership.</p>

<h3>Production</h3>

<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><u>Title to Properties </u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>The Partnership's interests in producing acreage are in
the form of assigned direct interests in leases. Such properties are subject to
customary royalty interests generally contracted for in connection with the
acquisition of properties and could be subject to liens incident to operating
agreements, liens for current taxes, and other burdens.&nbsp; The Partnership
believes that none of these burdens materially interfere with the use of such
properties in the operation of the Partnership's business.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>As
is customary in the oil and gas industry, little or no investigation of title
is made at the time of acquisition of undeveloped properties (other than a
preliminary review of local mineral records).&nbsp; Investigations are
generally made, including in most cases receiving a title opinion of legal
counsel, before commencement of drilling operations.&nbsp; A thorough
examination of title has been made with respect to all of the Partnership's
producing properties and the Partnership believes that it has satisfactory
title to such properties.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM
3.</u></b><b><u>&nbsp; LEGAL
PROCEEDINGS</u></b></p>



<p class=dmbodytext5 style='margin-bottom:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:
0in'>The Registrant is not a party to any legal proceedings.</p>



<p class=dmbodytext5 style='margin-bottom:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:
justify;text-indent:0in'>PDC, as Managing General Partner and operator of the
Partnership's wells, may be subject to various legal proceedings from time to
time arising in the normal course of business.&nbsp; Any outstanding and
pending legal actions are not considered material to the operations of the
Partnership or PDC.</p>

market ever develop for the interests.&nbsp; Limited and additional general
partnership interests are transferable, however no
assignee of an interest in the Partnership can become a substituted partner
without the written consent of the transferor and the Managing General Partner.

<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM
7.</u></b><b><u> MANAGEMENT'S DISCUSSION
AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoHeading7>Safe Harbor Statement Under the Private Securities
Litigation Reform Act of 1995</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>Statements, other than historical facts, contained in
this Annual Report on Form 10-K, including statements of estimated oil and gas
production and reserves, future cash flows and the Partnership's strategies,
plans and objectives, are &quot;forward-looking statements&quot; within the meaning of
Section 27A of the Securities Act of 1933, as amended (the &quot;Securities Act&quot;),
and Section 21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the
&quot;Exchange Act&quot;).&nbsp; Although the Partnership believes that its forward
looking statements are based on reasonable assumptions, it cautions that such
statements are subject to a wide range of risks, trends and uncertainties,
incidental to the production and marketing of oil and gas that could cause
actual results to differ materially from those projected.&nbsp; Among those
risks, trends and uncertainties are important factors that could cause actual
results to differ materially from the forward looking statements, including,
but not limited to, changes in production volumes, worldwide demand and
commodity prices for petroleum natural resources; risks incidental to the
operation of oil and gas wells; future production and development costs; the
effect of existing and future laws, governmental regulations and the political
and economic climate of the United States; the effect of derivative activities;
and conditions in the capital markets.&nbsp; In particular, careful
consideration should be given to cautionary statements made in this Form 10-K
and in the various reports the Partnership has filed with the Securities and
Exchange Commission.&nbsp; The Partnership undertakes no duty to update or revise
these forward-looking statements.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>When
used in this Form 10-K, the words, &quot;expect,&quot; &quot;anticipate,&quot; &quot;intend,&quot; &quot;plan,&quot;
&quot;believe,&quot; &quot;seek,&quot; &quot;estimate&quot; and similar expressions are intended to identify
forward-looking statements, although not all forward-looking statements contain
these identifying words. Because these forward-looking statements involve risks
and uncertainties, actual results could differ materially from those expressed
or implied by these forward-looking statements for a number of important reasons,
including those discussed under &quot;Item 1A - Risk Factors&quot;&nbsp; and elsewhere in
this Form 10-K.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'><u>Overview</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership was funded on February 9, 2005, with initial Investor Partner
contributions of $39,937,470 and the Managing General Partner's cash
contribution of $8,829,000.&nbsp; After payment of syndication costs of
$4,022,407 and a one-time management fee to the Managing General Partner of
$599,062, the Partnership had available cash of $44,145,001 to commence the
Partnership's drilling activities.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>-12-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
drilling of oil and gas wells on prospects evaluated and designated by PDC
commenced on March 5, 2005. Forty-nine wells have been drilled, and as of
December 31, 2005, forty-eight wells have been completed and are producing. The
completion work on one of the wells drilled in 2005 has been delayed until the
spring of 2006 due to weather conditions restricting access to the well site.
The Managing General Partner anticipates that the remaining uncompleted well
will be commercially productive upon completion. &nbsp;The Partnership drilled
only development wells and did not participate in the drilling of exploratory
wells.&nbsp; No additional wells will be drilled by the Partnership.&nbsp; The
table in &quot;Item 1 - Business&quot; above summarizes the Partnership's drilling
activity during 2005.</p>

referenced period in the Partnership's first year of operations:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:2.0in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:2.0in;text-align:justify'>* Definitions: </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:2.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Bbl - One barrel or
42 U.S. gallons of liquid volume.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:2.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Mcf - One thousand cubic feet.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:2.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Mcfe - One thousand cubic feet of
natural gas equivalents, based on a ratio of 6 Mcf
for each barrel of oil, which reflects the relative energy content.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Initial production from the Partnership wells commenced
during the second quarter of 2005, as wells were drilled, completed and
connected to pipelines. Sales of natural gas and oil from the Partnership's
wells increased steadily during 2005 as additional wells were completed and
placed into production.&nbsp; The last well to commence production during the
year occurred in the fourth quarter.&nbsp; The table below reflects the
production volumes, net to the Partnership, for each of the quarters in&nbsp;
2005.&nbsp; </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>-13-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The Partnership's future revenues from oil and natural
gas sales will be affected by changes in prices.&nbsp; As a result of changes
in market conditions, gas prices are highly dependent on the balance between
supply and demand. The Partnership's sales prices for natural gas and oil are
subject to increases and decreases based on various market sensitive indices.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>Interest income was earned by the Partnership during
2005 on bank balances that existed while awaiting capital expenditures on the
drilling of the remaining oil and gas wells.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>In accordance with the Partnership Agreement, a
one-time management fee equal to 1&frac12;% of investors' subscriptions, or $599,062,
was paid by the Partnership to the Managing General Partner upon funding of the
Partnership.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
net loss of $181,625 from oil and gas price risk management is comprised of the
change in fair value of oil and natural gas derivatives related to the
Partnership's oil and gas production for derivative contracts entered into on
behalf of the Partnership by the Managing General Partner.&nbsp; The
Partnership views these transactions as a gain or loss on financial instruments
and not a part of oil and gas sales.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><u>Liquidity and Capital Resources</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The Partnership had a working capital balance at December
31, 2005, of $5,745,650, which was primarily the result of receivables from oil
and gas sales during the fourth quarter. Future operations are expected to be
conducted with available funds and revenues generated from oil and gas
production activities.&nbsp; As of the date of this report, the Partnership has substantially finished the drilling and completion
of its 49 wells and all partner contributions will have been utilized in this
process.&nbsp; Other than the planned future
recompletions in the Codell
formation, there is no provision in the Partnership Agreement for
additional development or exploration beyond these 49 wells and there are no
present capital needs of the Partnership. Current production revenues exceed
operating costs by a wide margin. However, PDC plans to recomplete
the Codell formation in most of the 36 wells in the
Wattenberg Field after five years or more of production. These Codell recompletions typically increase the production rates and
recoverable reserves.&nbsp; Prior experience of PDC and other producers with Codell recompletions has resulted
in significant production increases for most wells, although not all recompletions have been successful. &nbsp;The cost
of a Codell recompletion is
about one-third of the cost of a new well (currently about $180,000 for the recompletion). The Partnership is not permitted to borrow
under the Partnership Agreement; therefore, the cost of the recompletions
will be paid out of overall revenues of the Partnership.&nbsp; The Managing
General Partner is allowed to and may withhold production revenues in advance
of recompletion work.&nbsp; This would reduce cash
distributions to the partners at the time of the recompletions,
but should result in additional cash distributions following the recompletions.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><u>Oil
and Gas Reserves</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Proved
oil and gas reserves of the Partnership have been estimated at December 31,
2005, to include 690,000 barrels of oil and 15,197,000 Mcfs
of natural gas.&nbsp; See &quot;Note 7 - Supplemental Reserve Information (Unaudited)&quot; in the Financial Statements for additional
reserve information.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Management's
Discussion and Analysis- Three Months Ended June 30, 2005</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Results
of Operation - </i>During the<i> </i>quarter,
the Partnership had net income of $615,697 resulting from the commencement of
production of oil and gas.&nbsp; Production commenced as wells were drilled,
completed and connected to a pipeline.&nbsp; During the quarter 26 wells began
producing. Total production for the Partnership during the quarter was 42,005 Mcf of gas and 20,562 barrels of oil. The results included
net losses related to oil and gas price risk management of $111,304 which
included an unrealized loss of $67,976 and a realized loss of $43,328.&nbsp;
The Partnership's strategy in its derivative policy is to provide protection on
declining oil and natural gas prices.&nbsp; During this period of rising oil
and natural gas prices, the Partnership recorded losses as market prices
exceeded contract prices related to the Partnership's oil and gas sales.&nbsp;
The Partnership made no partner cash distributions during the quarter.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Management's
Discussion and Analysis- Three Months Ended September 30, 2005</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Results
of Operation - </i>During the<i> </i>quarter,
the Partnership had net income of $1,477,379 as more wells commenced production
of oil and gas.&nbsp; During the quarter, 14 wells began producing and an
additional 8 wells were drilled, completed but not yet connected to a
pipeline.&nbsp; &nbsp;Only one well remained to be drilled at September 30,
2005, to complete the Partnership's drilling program.&nbsp; Total production
for the Partnership during the quarter was 185,654 Mcf
of gas and 45,694 barrels of oil. The results included net losses related to
oil and gas price risk management of $10,067 which included an unrealized gain
of $24,105 and a realized loss of $34,172.&nbsp; The Partnership's strategy in
its derivative policy is to provide protection on declining oil and natural gas
prices.&nbsp; During periods of rising oil and natural gas prices, the
Partnership may recorded losses as market prices exceed contract prices related
to the Partnership's derivatives.&nbsp; In periods of declining prices, the
Partnership may record gains in its derivative transactions.&nbsp; Partnership
revenue is affected by changes in oil and natural gas prices.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership distributed $1,079,425 to partners during the quarter.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='tab-stops:286.5pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>-15-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<h1>Critical Accounting Policies and Estimates</h1>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>We
have identified the following policies as critical to the understanding of the
results of operations. This is not a comprehensive list of all of our
accounting policies. In many cases, the accounting treatment of a particular
transaction is specifically dictated by accounting principles generally
accepted in the United States, with no need for management's judgment in their
application. There are also areas in which management's judgment in selecting
any available alternative would not produce a materially different result.
However, certain accounting policies are important to the portrayal of the
Partnership's financial condition and results of operations and require
management's most subjective or complex judgments. In applying those policies,
management uses its judgment to determine the appropriate assumptions to be
used in the determination of certain estimates. Those estimates are based on
our historical experience, our observance of trends in the industry, and
information available from other outside sources, as appropriate. For a more
detailed discussion on the application of these and other accounting policies,
see &quot;Note 2 - Summary of Significant Accounting Policies&quot; and other related
notes in the Financial Statements. The Partnership's critical accounting
policies and estimates are as follows:</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Oil
and Gas Properties </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The Partnership accounts for its oil and gas properties
under the successful efforts method of accounting.&nbsp; Costs of proved
developed producing properties, successful exploratory wells and development
dry hole costs are depreciated or depleted by the unit-of-production method
based on estimated proved developed producing oil and gas reserves.&nbsp;
Property acquisition costs are depreciated or depleted on the
unit-of-production method based on estimated proved oil and gas reserves.&nbsp;
The Partnership obtains new reserve reports from independent petroleum
engineers annually as of December 31st of each year.&nbsp; The Partnership
adjusts for any major acquisitions, new drilling and divestures during the year
as needed.&nbsp; The Partnership does not maintain an inventory of undrilled leases.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-right:-4.5pt;text-align:justify'>Upon sale or retirement of
significant or entire portions of fields of depreciable or depletable
property, the book value thereof, less proceeds, is credited or charged to
income.&nbsp; Upon sale of a partial unit of property, the proceeds are
credited to accumulated depreciation and depletion.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Use
of Estimates in Testing for Impairment in Long-Lived Assets</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-right:-4.5pt;text-align:justify'>Impairment testing for long-lived
assets is required when circumstances indicate those assets may be
impaired.&nbsp; The Partnership assesses impairment of capitalized costs of
proved oil and gas properties by comparing net capitalized costs to the
estimated undiscounted future net cash flows on a field-by-field basis using
estimated production and based upon prices at which management reasonably
estimates such products will be sold. These estimates of future product prices
may differ from current market prices of oil and gas. Any downward revisions to
the Partnership's estimates of future production or product prices could result
in an impairment of the Partnership's oil and gas properties in subsequent
periods. If net capitalized costs exceed undiscounted future net cash flows,
the measurement of impairment is based on estimated fair value calculated using
future discounted cash flows.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Revenue
Recognition</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Sales
of natural gas are recognized when natural gas has been delivered to a custody
transfer point, persuasive evidence of a sales arrangement exists, the rights
and responsibility of ownership pass to the purchaser, collection of revenue
from the sale is reasonably assured, and the sales price is fixed or
determinable.&nbsp; Natural gas is sold by the Managing General Partner under
contracts with terms ranging from one month up to the life of the well.&nbsp;
Virtually all of the Managing General Partner's contracts' pricing provisions
are tied to a market index with certain adjustments based on, among other
factors, whether a well delivers to a gathering or transmission line, quality
of natural gas and prevailing supply and demand conditions, so that the price
of the natural gas fluctuates to remain competitive with other available
natural gas supplies.&nbsp; As a result, the Partnership's revenues from the
sale of natural gas will suffer if market prices decline and benefit if they
increase.&nbsp; However, the Managing General Partner may from time to time
enter into derivative agreements, usually with a term of two years or less which
may either fix or collar a price in order to reduce market price fluctuations.
The Partnership believes that the pricing provisions of its natural gas
contracts are customary in the industry. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:center;
text-indent:-9.0pt'>-16-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='page-break-before:always'>




<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Managing General Partner currently uses the &quot;Net-Back&quot; method of accounting for
transportation arrangements of natural gas sales.&nbsp; The Managing General
Partner sells gas at the wellhead and collects a price and recognizes revenues
based on the wellhead sales price since transportation costs downstream of the wellhead
are incurred by the Managing General Partner's customers and reflected in the
wellhead price.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Sales
of oil are recognized when persuasive evidence of a sales arrangement exists,
the oil is verified as produced and is delivered from a stock tank to a purchaser,
collection of revenue from the sale is reasonably assured, and the sales price
is determinable.&nbsp; The Partnership does not refine any of its oil
production.&nbsp; The Partnership's crude oil production is sold to purchasers
at or near the Partnership's wells under short-term purchase contracts at
prices and in accordance with arrangements that are customary in the oil
industry.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><u>Derivative
Financial Instruments</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership accounts for derivative financial instruments in accordance with
FAS Statement No. 133 &quot;Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Certain
Hedging Activities&quot; as amended.&nbsp; During 2005, none of the derivative
contracts qualified for hedge accounting under the terms of FAS No. 133.&nbsp;
Accordingly, the derivative instruments are recorded as an asset or liability
on the balance sheet at fair value and the change in the fair value is recorded
in oil and gas price risk management loss (gain), net.&nbsp; Because derivative
arrangements are entered into by the Managing General Partner on behalf of the
Partnership, the fair value of open derivative positions is reported on the
balance sheet as a net short-term or long-term receivable due from or payable
due to the Managing General Partner.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The measurement of fair value is based on actively quoted
market prices, if available. Otherwise, the Managing General Partner seeks
indicative price information from external sources including broker quotes and
industry publications. If pricing information from external sources is not
available, measurement involves judgment and estimates. These estimates are
based on valuation methodologies considered appropriate by the Managing General
Partner. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>By using derivative financial instruments to manage
exposures to changes in commodity prices, the Partnership exposes itself to
credit risk.&nbsp; Credit risk is the failure of the counterparty to perform
under the terms of the derivative contract.&nbsp; When the fair value of a
derivative contract is positive, the counterparty owes the Managing General
Partner, which in turn owes the Partnership thus creating repayment risk.&nbsp;
The Managing General Partner minimizes the credit or repayment risk in
derivative instruments by entering into transactions with high-quality
counterparties.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><u>Recently
Issued Accounting Standards</u></p>



<p class=MsoBodyTextIndent style='text-indent:0in'>In June 2005, the FASB
issued SFAS No. 154, &quot;Accounting Changes and Error Corrections&quot; - a
replacement of APB Opinion No. 20 and FASB Statement No. 3, which replaces
Accounting Principles Board Opinion No. 20, &quot;Accounting Changes,&quot; and
SFAS No. 3, &quot;Reporting Accounting Changes in Interim Financial
Statements,&quot; and changes the requirements for the accounting for and
reporting of a change in accounting principle. SFAS No. 154 requires
retrospective application for voluntary changes in accounting principle unless
it is impracticable to do so, and it applies to all voluntary changes in
accounting principle. &nbsp;SFAS No. 154 is effective for accounting changes
and corrections of errors made in fiscal years beginning after December 15,
2005. Consequently, we will adopt the provisions of SFAS 154 for our fiscal
year beginning January 1, 2006. We currently believe that adoption of the
provisions of SFAS No. 154 will not have a material impact on our financial
statements.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>Item
7A.&nbsp;&nbsp;Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosure About Market Risk</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Market-Sensitive
Instruments and Risk Management</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership's primary market risk exposure is commodity price risk for the oil
and gas the Partnership produces and sells.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><u>Commodity Price Risk</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Managing General Partner utilizes commodity-based derivative instruments,
entered into on behalf of the Partnership, to manage a portion of the
Partnership's exposure to price risk from oil and natural gas sales.&nbsp;
These instruments consist of CIG (Colorado Interstate Gas) index-based
contracts traded by JP Morgan for Colorado natural gas production. These
derivative instruments have the effect of locking in for specified periods (at
predetermined prices or ranges of prices) the prices the Managing General
Partner will receive for the volume of oil and natural gas to which the
derivative relates.&nbsp; As a result, while these derivative instruments are
structured to reduce Partnership's exposure
to changes in price associated with the derivative commodity, they also limit
the benefit the Partnership might otherwise have received from price changes
associated with the commodity.&nbsp; The Partnership has adopted the policy of
the Managing General Partner prohibiting the use of oil and natural gas future
and option contracts for speculative purposes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>-17-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='page-break-before:always'>




<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.35pt'>Derivative arrangements are entered into
by the Managing General Partner on behalf of the Partnership and are reported
on the Partnership's balance sheet at fair value as a net short-term or
long-term receivable due from or payable to the Managing General Partner.&nbsp;
Changes in the fair value of the Partnership's share of derivatives are
recorded in the statement of operations. The following table summarizes the
open derivative positions for the Partnership as of December 31, 2005.</p>



<div align=center>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
annual average Colorado Interstate Gas closing price for natural gas for 2005
was $6.96 per Mmbtu.&nbsp; The average NYMEX closing
price for oil for 2005 was $55.34 per barrel.&nbsp; Future near-term gas and
oil prices will be affected by various supply and demand factors such as
weather, government and environmental regulations and new drilling activities
within the industry.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Disclosure of Limitations</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>As
the information above incorporates only those exposures that exist at December
31, 2005, it does not consider those exposures or positions which could arise
after that date. As a result, the Partnership's ultimate realized gain or loss
with respect to commodity price fluctuations will depend on the exposures that
arise during the period, the Partnership's hedging strategies at the time and
commodity prices at the time.</p>
