<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><b><u>ITEM 9.&nbsp;&nbsp;CHANGES IN AND DISAGREEMENTS WITH ACCOUNTANTS ON
ACCOUNTING AND</u></b><b> <u>FINANCIAL
DISCLOSURE</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'>None.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM 9A. CONTROLS AND
PROCEDURES&nbsp; </u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Introductory
Explanation</i> - As disclosed in more
detail in &quot;Item 1 - Business&quot; above, the Partnership has no management or officers
because all of the management, officers and other employees that may provide
services to or on behalf of the Partnership are employed by the Managing
General Partner.&nbsp; As used for the disclosures in this Item 9A, management
and officers of the Partnership refers to the management and officers of the
Managing General Partner.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Evaluation
of disclosure controls and procedures</i>
- - The Partnership carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the
participation of management including the Chief Executive Officer and the Chief
Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of its
disclosure controls and procedures pursuant to Exchange Act Rule 13a-14(a) as
of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K. Based upon
and as of the date of this evaluation, the Chief Executive Officer and the
Chief Financial Officer concluded that as of the date of this report, the
Partnership's disclosure controls and procedures were not effective because of
the material weaknesses described below.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Material
weaknesses in internal control - </i>During
2005, the Partnership identified material weaknesses related
to its policies and procedures and technical expertise in U.S. generally
accepted accounting principles to ensure the preparation of accurate and
reliable interim and annual financial statements. Specifically, the Partnership
lacked personnel with sufficient technical accounting and financial reporting
expertise and policies and procedures in place to determine and document the
appropriate application of accounting principles. These deficiencies impacted
the Partnership's accounting for derivatives, asset retirement obligations and
depreciation, depletion and amortization, and result in more than a remote
likelihood that a material misstatement of the annual or interim financial
statements would not be prevented or detected.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>In
light of the material weaknesses described above, the Partnership performed
additional analyses and other post-closing procedures to ensure its financial
statements are prepared in accordance with generally accepted accounting
principles. Accordingly, notwithstanding the material weaknesses discussed in
this Item 9A, management believes that the financial statements included in
this report fairly present in all material respects our financial position,
results of operations and cash flows for the periods presented. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'><i>&nbsp;</i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'><i>Changes in internal control over financial reporting</i> - </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>There
have not been any changes in the Partnership's internal control over financial
reporting (as such term is defined in Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) of the
Securities Exchange Act of 1934) during the most recent fiscal quarter that
have materially affected or are reasonably likely to materially affect internal
control over financial reporting, except for changes in the fourth quarter of
2005 as noted below.&nbsp; </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The Partnership
has increased its technical expertise through development of training programs
and acquisition of accounting research software during the fourth quarter of
2005.&nbsp; Training will be on-going; however, programs provided during 2005
included oil and gas accounting, general accounting and SEC financial
reporting.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The Partnership
has enhanced the documentation of its policies and procedures and related
templates and analyses that support the application of accounting principles in
several areas, including derivatives, oil and gas properties, and asset
retirement obligations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.25in'>-19-</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>In addition, during the third quarter of fiscal 2005
and subsequently in 2006, the Partnership made the following changes and
remediation:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>At the direction of the board of directors and audit
committee, the Partnership has spent and continues to spend a significant
amount of time and resources to improve its control environment.&nbsp; The
Partnership is committed to instilling strong internal control policies and
procedures and ensuring that the &quot;tone at the top&quot; fully supports
accuracy and completeness in all financial reporting.&nbsp; In support of this
position, the Partnership's progress toward improving internal control over
financial reporting has been openly communicated with the Audit Committee, and
the Partnership has undertaken to improve the design and effectiveness of its
internal control over financial reporting. The initiatives developed were both
organizational and process focused.&nbsp; Organizational changes made during
2005 and through the date of this filing include, among others:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The Partnership has enhanced the corporate accounting and reporting functions
in the third quarter of 2005 by creating and filling several new positions with
professionals highly experienced in oil and gas accounting. Two new
professionals hold degrees in accounting and are Certified Public Accountants.
One additional Certified Public Accountant and a financial reporting director
were hired during 2006.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The Partnership engaged a team of highly experienced advisors in early 2006 to
assist with various accounting research, projects and monitoring
activities.&nbsp; They assist with accounting and reporting issues including,
but not limited to, derivatives, oil and gas activities, new accounting
standards or rules, SEC reporting and on-going monitoring of changes that may impact
the Partnership's application of accounting principles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The Partnership began the process of implementing measures related to
documentation of its controls and procedures, segregation of duties, timely
reconciliations and the use of disclosure checklists to support the financial
reporting process.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>The Partnership has also implemented or is planning to
implement several process changes to improve the documentation supporting
certain accounting and reporting activities as well as to improve the documentation
of its application of accounting principles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.75in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The Partnership has evaluated and selected a third-party integrated oil and gas
accounting software system, which it plans to implement during 2006.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify'>The Partnership believes the measures taken to date
and planned for the future will address the reported material weaknesses and
intends to complete the remediation efforts during 2006.&nbsp; In addition, the
Partnership will continue to develop and implement other initiatives during
2006 that will further improve both the effectiveness and efficiency of its
internal control over financial reporting. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>Beginning with the fiscal year ending December 31,
2007, Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002 will require us to include
an internal control report of management with our Annual Report on Form 10-K.
The internal control report must contain (1) a statement of management's
responsibility for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over
financial reporting, (2) a statement identifying the framework used by
management to conduct the required evaluation of the effectiveness of our
internal control over financial reporting, (3) management's assessment of the
effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting as of the end of
our most recent fiscal year, including a statement as to whether or not our
internal control over financial reporting is effective, and (4) a statement
that our independent registered public accountants have issued an attestation
report on management's assessment of our internal control over financial
reporting.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>In order to achieve compliance with Section 404 within
the prescribed period, management has begun to assess the adequacy of our
internal control over financial reporting, remediate any control weaknesses
that may be identified, and implement a continuous reporting and improvement
process for internal control over financial reporting. We expect to continue to
make changes in our internal control over financial reporting during the
periods prior to December 31, 2007, in connection with our Section 404
compliance efforts. Except as described above, there have been no changes in
our internal control over financial reporting (as defined in Rule 13(a)-15(f)
under the Exchange Act) that occurred during the quarters ended June 30, 2005,
September 30, 2005 and December 31, 2005, that have materially affected or are
reasonably likely to materially affect our internal control over financial
reporting. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center;text-autospace:none'>-20-</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>&nbsp;</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;text-autospace:none'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'><i>Limitations
on the effectiveness of internal control.</i> A control system, no matter how well conceived and operated, can
provide only reasonable, not absolute, assurance that the objectives of the
internal control system are met. Because of the inherent limitations of any internal
control system, no evaluation of controls can provide absolute assurance that
all control issues, if any, within a company have been detected.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><b><u>ITEM 9B.&nbsp; OTHER INFORMATION</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>None.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'><b><u>PART III</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM 10. DIRECTORS AND
EXECUTIVE OFFICERS OF THE REGISTRANT</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership has no directors or executive officers.&nbsp; The Partnership is
managed by Petroleum Development Corporation (&quot;PDC&quot;), the Managing General
Partner.&nbsp; PDC's common stock is listed on the
NASDAQ Global Select Market and Form 10-K for 2005 has been filed with the
Securities and Exchange Commission.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>Although
the Partnership has no Code of Ethics, PDC has a Code of Ethics that applies to
its senior executive officers.&nbsp; The Code of Ethics, and other information
related to PDC, is posted on PDC's website at
www.petd.com. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal><b><u>ITEM 11.&nbsp;
EXECUTIVE COMPENSATION</u></b></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>The
Partnership, having no executive officers or directors, pays no executive
compensation.&nbsp; None of PDC's officers or
directors received any direct remuneration or other compensation from the
Partnership. These persons receive remuneration and compensation solely from
PDC.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><b><u>ITEM 12.&nbsp; SECURITY OWNERSHIP OF CERTAIN BENEFICIAL OWNERS AND

<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'>The
Partnership has no equity compensation plans.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'>PDC
owns a 20% partnership interest in the Partnership.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><b><u>ITEM 14.&nbsp;&nbsp;PRINCIPAL ACCOUNTANT FEES AND SERVICES </u></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='page-break-after:avoid'><u>Pre-Approval Policies and Procedures</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'>The Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002 requires that all
services provided to the Partnership by its independent accountants be subject to
pre-approval by the Audit Committee or authorized members of the Committee. The
Partnership does not have an Audit Committee; however, the Managing General
Partner's Audit Committee also serves for the Partnership.&nbsp; The Audit
Committee has adopted policies and procedures for pre-approval of all audit
services and non-audit services to be provided by the Partnership's independent
accountants. Actual fees incurred for all services performed by the independent
accountant are reported to the Audit Committee after the services are fully
performed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>F-2</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>



<p class=ind>Report of Independent Registered Public Accounting Firm</p>



<p class=MsoBodyText>To the Partners</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>PDC 2005-A Limited Partnership:</p>





<p class=MsoBodyText>We have audited the accompanying balance sheet of PDC 2005-A
Limited Partnership as of December 31, 2005, and the related statements of
operations, partners' equity and cash flows for the period from February 9,
2005 (date of inception) to December 31, 2005.&nbsp; These financial statements
are the responsibility of the Partnership's management.&nbsp; Our
responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on
our audit.</p>



<p class=MsoBodyText>We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of
the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).&nbsp; Those
standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable
assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material
misstatement.&nbsp; An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence
supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements.&nbsp; An
audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant
estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial
statement presentation.&nbsp; We believe that our audit provides a reasonable
basis for our opinion.</p>



<p class=MsoBodyText>In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above
present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of PDC 2005-A
Limited Partnership as of December 31, 2005, and the results of its operations
and its cash flows for the period from February 9, 2005 (date of inception) to
December 31, 2005, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting
principles.</p>



<p class=MsoBodyText>KPMG LLP</p>





<p class=MsoBodyText>Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>July 20, 2006</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>F-7</p>





<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in;page-break-after:avoid'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in;page-break-after:avoid'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in;page-break-after:avoid'>(1)&nbsp;&nbsp; <u>Organization</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt;page-break-after:avoid'>The PDC 2005-A
Limited Partnership (the &quot;Partnership&quot;) was organized as a limited partnership
in accordance with the laws of the State of West Virginia for the purpose of
engaging in the drilling, completion and operation of oil and gas development
and exploratory wells in the Rocky Mountain Region. Business operations of the
Partnership commenced on February 9, 2005, upon the closing of an offering for
the sale of partnership units.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Purchasers of partnership units
subscribed to and fully paid for 124.79 units of limited partner interests and
1,872.08 units of additional general partner interests at $20,000 per unit.
Petroleum Development Corporation (&quot;PDC&quot;) has been designated the Managing
General Partner of the Partnership.&nbsp; Generally, throughout the term of the
Partnership, revenues, costs and cash available for distributions are allocated
80% to the limited and additional general partners pro rata based on their
investment in the Partnership and 20% to the Managing General Partner.&nbsp;
The limited and additional general partners are referred to collectively as
&quot;Investor Partners.&quot;</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>In accordance with the terms of the
Limited Partnership Agreement (the &quot;Agreement&quot;), the Managing General Partner
manages all activities of the Partnership and acts as the intermediary for substantially
all Partnership transactions.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-indent:-.25in'>&nbsp;(2)&nbsp; <u>Summary of Significant Accounting
Policies</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'><u>Partnership Financial Statement
Presentation Basis</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The financial statements include only those
assets, liabilities and results of operations of the partners which relate to
the business of the Partnership.&nbsp; The statements do not include any
assets, liabilities, revenues or expenses attributable to any of the partners'
other activities. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'><u>Oil and Gas Properties</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Partnership
accounts for its oil and gas properties under the successful efforts method of
accounting. Costs of proved developed producing properties and development dry
hole costs are depreciated or depleted by the unit-of-production method based
on estimated proved developed producing oil and gas reserves.&nbsp; Property
acquisition costs are depreciated or depleted on the unit-of-production method
based on estimated proved oil and gas reserves.&nbsp; The Partnership obtains
new reserve reports from independent petroleum engineers annually as of
December 31st of each year.&nbsp; The Partnership adjusts for any major
acquisitions, new drilling and divestures during the year as needed.&nbsp; The
Partnership does not maintain an inventory of undrilled
leases.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Upon sale or
retirement of significant or entire portions of fields of depreciable or depletable property, the book value thereof less proceeds,
is credited or charged to income.&nbsp; Upon sale of a partial unit of
property, the proceeds are credited to accumulated depreciation and depletion.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Impairment of
Long-Lived Assets</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Impairment testing
for long-lived assets is required when circumstances indicate those assets may
be impaired.&nbsp; The Partnership assesses impairment of capitalized costs of
proved oil and gas properties by comparing net capitalized costs to estimated
undiscounted future net cash flows on a field-by-field basis using estimated
production based upon prices at which management reasonably estimates such
products will be sold. These estimates of future product prices may differ from
current market prices of oil and gas. Any downward revisions to the
Partnership's estimates of future production or product prices could result in
an impairment of the Partnership's oil and gas properties in subsequent
periods. If net capitalized costs exceed undiscounted future net cash flows, an
impairment is recorded.&nbsp; The measurement of impairment is based on
estimated fair value which may consider future discounted cash flows.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>F-8</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'><u>Revenue Recognition</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Sales of natural gas are recognized when
natural gas has been delivered to a custody transfer point, persuasive evidence
of a sales arrangement exists, the rights and responsibility of ownership pass
to the purchaser upon delivery, collection of revenue from the sale is
reasonably assured, and the sales price is fixed or determinable.&nbsp; Natural
gas is sold by the Managing General Partner under contracts with terms ranging
from one month up to the life of the well (see Note 3).&nbsp; Virtually all of
the Managing General Partner's contracts pricing provisions are tied to a
market index with certain adjustments based on, among other factors, whether a
well delivers to a gathering or transmission line, quality of natural gas and
prevailing supply and demand conditions, so that the price of the natural gas
fluctuates to remain competitive with other available natural gas
supplies.&nbsp; As a result, the Partnership's revenues from the sale of
natural gas will suffer if market prices decline and benefit if they increase.&nbsp;
However, the Managing General Partner may from time to time enter into
derivative agreements, usually with a term of two years or less which may
either fix or collar a price in order to reduce market price fluctuations. The
Partnership believes that the pricing provisions of its natural gas contracts
are customary in the industry. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Managing General Partner currently
uses the &quot;Net-Back&quot; method of accounting for transportation arrangements of
natural gas sales.&nbsp; The Managing General Partner sells gas at the wellhead
and collects a price and recognizes revenues based on the wellhead sales price
since transportation costs downstream of the wellhead are incurred by the
Managing General Partner's customers and reflected in the wellhead price.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Sales of oil are recognized when
persuasive evidence of a sales arrangement exists, the oil is verified as
produced and is delivered in a stock tank, collection of revenue from the sale
is reasonably assured and the sales price is determinable.&nbsp; The
Partnership is currently able to sell all the oil that it can produce under
existing sales contracts with petroleum refiners and marketers.&nbsp; The
Partnership does not refine any of its oil production.&nbsp; The Partnership's
crude oil production is sold to purchasers at or near the Partnership's wells
under short-term purchase contracts at prices and in accordance with
arrangements that are customary in the oil industry.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Partnership sold oil and natural gas
to three customers, during 2005, which accounted for 49%, 33% and 18% of the
Partnership's total oil and natural gas sales for the period.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.35pt'><u>Asset
Retirement Obligations</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.35pt'>The Partnership accounts for asset
retirement obligations by recording the fair value of its plugging and abandonment
obligations when incurred, which is at the time the well is completely drilled.
Upon initial recognition of an asset retirement obligation, the Partnership
increases the carrying amount of the long-lived asset by the same amount as the
liability. Over time, asset retirement obligations are accreted for the change
in their present value. The initial capitalized costs are depleted over the useful lives of the related assets,
through charges to depreciation, depletion and amortization. </p>

<h4>&nbsp;</h4>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'><u>Derivative Financial Instruments</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Partnership accounts for derivative
financial instruments in accordance with FAS Statement No. 133 &quot;Accounting
for Derivative Instruments and Certain Hedging Activities&quot; as
amended.&nbsp; During 2005, none of the derivative contracts qualified for
hedge accounting under the terms of FAS No. 133.&nbsp; Accordingly, the
derivative instruments are recorded as an asset or liability on the balance
sheet at fair value and the change in the fair value is recorded in oil and gas
price risk management loss (gain), net.&nbsp; Because derivative arrangements
are entered into by the Managing General Partner on behalf of the Partnership,
the fair value of open derivative positions is reported on the balance sheet as
a net short-term or long-term receivable due from or payable due to the
Managing General Partner.&nbsp; Amounts due to the Managing General Partner for
realized losses and gains on closed derivative positions are included in
accounts payable in the amount of $81,537 at December 31, 2005. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The measurement of fair value is based
on actively quoted market prices, if available. Otherwise, the Managing General
Partner seeks indicative price information from external sources including
broker quotes and industry publications. If pricing information from external
sources is not available, measurement involves judgment and estimates. These
estimates are based on valuation methodologies considered appropriate by the
Managing General Partner. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:center;
text-indent:-9.0pt'>F-9</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>By using derivative financial
instruments to manage exposures to changes in commodity prices, the Partnership
exposes itself to credit risk.&nbsp; Credit risk is the failure of the
counterparty to perform under the terms of the derivative contract.&nbsp; When
the fair value of a derivative contract is positive, the counterparty owes the
Managing General Partner, which in turn owes the Partnership.&nbsp; The
Managing General Partner minimizes this credit risk by entering into
transactions with high-quality counterparties.</p>





<h4 style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-indent:-9.35pt'>Income Taxes</h4>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.35pt;page-break-after:avoid'>Since the
taxable income or loss of the Partnership is reported in the separate tax
returns of the partners, no provision has been made for income taxes on the
Partnership's books.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'><u>Use of Estimates</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Partnership has made a number of estimates
and assumptions relating to the reporting of assets and liabilities and
revenues and expenses and the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities
to prepare these financial statements in conformity with accounting principles
generally accepted in the United States of America. Actual results could differ
from those estimates. Estimates which are particularly significant to the
financial statements include estimates of oil and gas reserves and future cash
flows from oil and gas properties which are used in assessing impairment of
long-lived assets.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='text-autospace:none'><u>Fair
Value of Financial Instruments</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt;text-autospace:none'>The carrying values
of the Company's receivables, payables and debt obligations are estimated to be
substantially the same as the fair values as of December 31, 2005.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt;page-break-after:avoid'><u>Recently
Issued Accounting Standards</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.35pt;page-break-after:avoid'>In June 2005, the FASB issued SFAS No. 154, &quot;Accounting Changes and
Error Corrections&quot; - a replacement of APB Opinion No. 20 and FASB
Statement No. 3, which replaces Accounting Principles Board Opinion No. 20,
&quot;Accounting Changes,&quot; and SFAS No. 3, &quot;Reporting Accounting
Changes in Interim Financial Statements,&quot; and changes the requirements for
the accounting for and reporting of a change in accounting principle. SFAS No.
154 requires retrospective application for voluntary changes in accounting
principle unless it is impracticable to do so, and it applies to all voluntary
changes in accounting principle. SFAS No. 154 is effective for accounting
changes and corrections of errors made in fiscal years beginning after December
15, 2005. Consequently, we will adopt the provisions of SFAS 154 for our fiscal
year beginning January 1, 2006. We currently believe that adoption of the
provisions of SFAS No. 154 will not have a material impact on our financial
statements.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>In addition, as the operator of the
Partnership's wells, the Managing General Partner receives all &nbsp;proceeds
from the sale of oil and gas produced and pays for all costs incurred related
to services, equipment and supplies from vendors for all well production and
operating costs and other direct costs for the Partnership.&nbsp; Net revenue
from oil and gas operations is generally distributed monthly to all partners
based on their share of costs and revenues.&nbsp; </p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:center;
text-indent:-9.0pt'>F-10</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>As described above, the Managing General Partner
utilizes commodity-based derivative instruments, entered into on behalf of the
Partnership, to manage a portion of the Partnership's exposure to price risk
from oil and natural gas sales.&nbsp; These instruments consist of CIG
(Colorado Interstate Gas) index-based contracts traded by JP Morgan for
Colorado natural gas production. These derivative instruments have the effect of
locking in for specified periods (at predetermined prices or ranges of prices)
the prices the Managing General Partner will receive for the volume of oil and
natural gas to which the derivative relates.&nbsp; </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt;page-break-after:
avoid'>The fair value of the commodity based
derivatives was $(22,588) at December 31, 2005.&nbsp; The Partnership
recognized in the statement of operations a realized loss on commodity based
derivatives of $159,037 for the year ended December 31, 2005.&nbsp; The
following table summarizes the open derivative positions for the Partnership as
of December 31, 2005.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>(a)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Managing General Partner paid all
legal, accounting, printing, and filing fees associated with the organization
of the Partnership and the offering of units and is allocated 100% of these
costs.&nbsp; The Investor Partners paid all dealer manager commissions,
discounts, and due diligence reimbursements and are allocated 100% of these
costs. </p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>(b)&nbsp;&nbsp;Represents a one-time fee paid to the
Managing General Partner upon the funding of the Partnership equal to 1-1/2% of
total Investor Partner subscriptions.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>(c)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Represents operating costs
incurred after the completion of productive wells, including monthly per-well
charges paid to the Managing General Partner for well tending fees and
Partnership administration fees.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>(d)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Managing General Partner is
reimbursed by the Partnership for direct costs incurred by the Managing General
Partner on behalf of the Partnership, such as for independent auditor, reserve
engineer and tax preparation fees.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'>(e)&nbsp;&nbsp;To the extent that Investor Partners
receive preferred cash distributions, the allocations for Investor Partners
will be increased accordingly and the allocation for the Managing General
Partner will likewise be decreased.&nbsp; See &quot;Performance Standard Obligation
of Managing General Partner&quot; below.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal><u>Performance Standard
Obligation of Managing General Partner</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>The Agreement provides for the
enhancement of investor cash distributions if the Partnership does not meet a
performance standard defined in the Agreement during the first 10 years
beginning 6 months after the close of the Partnership.&nbsp; In general, if the
average annual rate of return to the Investor Partners is less than 12.5% of
their subscriptions, the allocation rate of cash distributions to Investor
Partners will increase by one-half of the Managing General Partner's interest
until the average annual rate increases to 12.5%, with a corresponding decrease
to the Managing General Partner.&nbsp; The 12.5% rate of return is calculated
by including the estimated benefit of a 25% income tax savings on the
investment in the first year in addition to cash distributions made to the
Investor Partners.&nbsp; During 2005, no obligation of the Managing General
Partner arose under this provision.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:center;
text-indent:-9.0pt'>F-12</p>

<hr color="#000080"><br clear=all style='mso-special-character:line-break;
page-break-before:always'>


<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>PDC 2005-A LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;(A West Virginia Limited Partnership)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>Notes to Financial Statements</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-indent:-9.0pt'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-indent:-9.35pt;page-break-after:
avoid'><u>Unit Repurchase Provisions</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.35pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.35pt;page-break-after:avoid'>Investor
Partners may request that the Managing General Partner repurchase units at any
time beginning with the third anniversary of the first cash distribution of the
Partnership.&nbsp; The repurchase price is set at a minimum of four times the
most recent twelve months' of cash distributions from production.&nbsp; The
Managing General Partner is obligated to purchase in any calendar year Investor
Partner units aggregating to 10% of the initial subscriptions if requested by
the Investor Partners, subject to its financial ability to do so and opinions
of counsel.&nbsp; No partnership units can be purchased under this provision by
the Managing General Partner until 2008.</p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:18.2pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in'>(7)&nbsp;&nbsp; <u>Supplemental Reserve
Information (Unaudited)</u></p>



<p class=MsoBodyTextIndent3>Proved oil and gas reserves of the Partnership have
been estimated at December 31, 2005, by independent petroleum engineers. These
reserves have been prepared in compliance with the Securities and Exchange
Commission rules based on year end prices. All of the Partnership's reserves
are proved developed reserves.&nbsp; An analysis of the change in estimated
quantities of proved developed oil and gas reserves is shown below:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -.25in;page-break-after:avoid'>(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;
<u>Standardized Measure of Discounted Future Net Cash Flows and Changes Therein
Relating to Proved Oil</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify;page-break-after:avoid'><u>and Gas Reserves (Unaudited)</u></p>



<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>Summarized in the following
table is information for the Partnership with respect to the standardized
measure of discounted future net cash flows relating to proved oil and gas reserves.&nbsp;
Future cash inflows are computed by applying year-end prices of oil and gas
relating to the Partnership's proved reserves to the year-end quantities of
those reserves.&nbsp; Future production, development, site restoration and
abandonment costs are derived based on current costs assuming continuation of
existing economic conditions. </p>

  <td width=16 nowrap valign=top style='width:11.8pt;padding:0in .85pt 0in .85pt;
  height:13.5pt'>
  <p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>
  </td>
  <td width=105 nowrap valign=top style='width:78.6pt;padding:0in .85pt 0in .85pt;
  height:13.5pt'>
  <p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>
  </td>
  <td width=16 nowrap valign=top style='width:11.8pt;padding:0in .85pt 0in .85pt;
  height:13.5pt'>
  <p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</table>

</div>

<p class=MsoNormal align=center style='text-align:center'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:9.0pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:
- -9.0pt'>It is necessary to emphasize that the
data presented should not be viewed as representing the expected cash flow
from, or current value of, existing proved reserves since the computations are
based on a large number of estimates and arbitrary assumptions.&nbsp; Reserve
quantities cannot be measured with precision and their estimation requires many
judgmental determinations and frequent revisions.&nbsp; The required projection
of production and related expenditures over time requires further estimates
with respect to pipeline availability, rates of demand and governmental control.
Actual future prices and costs are likely to be substantially different from
the current prices and costs utilized in the computation of reported
amounts.&nbsp; Any analysis or evaluation of the reported amounts should give
specific recognition to the computational methods utilized and the limitations
inherent therein.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='text-align:justify'>&nbsp;</p>

<title>Exhibit 31</title>

<body lang=EN-US>



<p align=right style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:right'>Exhibit 31.1</p>

<p align=center style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:center'><b>CERTIFICATION</b></p>



<p style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'>I,
Steven R. Williams, certify that:</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
I have reviewed this Annual Report on
Form 10-K of the Registrant:</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Based on my knowledge, this report does
not contain any untrue statement of a material fact or omit to state a material
fact necessary to make the statements made, in light of the circumstances under
which such statements were made, not misleading with respect to the period
covered by this report;</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Based on my knowledge, the financial
statements, and other financial information included in this report, fairly
present in all material respects the financial condition, results of operations
and cash flows of the registrant as of, and for, the periods presented in this
report;</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The registrant's other certifying officer
and I are responsible for establishing and maintaining disclosure controls and
procedures (as defined in Exchange Act Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e)) for the
registrant and have:</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>a.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Designed such disclosure controls
and procedures, or caused such disclosure controls and procedures to be
designed under our supervision, to ensure that material information relating to
the registrant, is made known to us by others within those entities,
particularly during the period in which this report is being prepared;</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>b.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Evaluated
the effectiveness of the registrant's disclosure controls and procedures and
presented in this report our conclusions about the effectiveness of the
disclosure controls and procedures, as of the end of the period covered by this
report based on such evaluation; and</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>c.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Disclosed
in this report any change in the registrant's internal control over financial
reporting that occurred during the registrant's most recent fiscal quarter (the
registrant's fourth fiscal quarter in the case of an annual report) that has
materially affected, or is reasonably likely to materially affect, the
registrant's internal control over financial reporting; and</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
The registrant's other certifying officer
and I have disclosed, based on our most recent evaluation of internal control
over financial reporting, to the registrant's auditor and the audit committee
of the registrant's board of directors (or persons performing the equivalent
functions);</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>a.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
All significant deficiencies and material
weaknesses in the design or operation of internal control over financial
reporting which are reasonably likely to adversely affect the registrant's
ability to record, process, summarize and report financial information; and</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>b.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Any fraud, whether or not material, that
involves management or other employees who have a significant role in the
registrant's internal control over financial reporting.</p>



<p style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'>Date:&nbsp;
September 7, 2006</p>

the registrant, is made known to us by others within those entities,

<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;

the registrant's internal control over financial reporting that occurred during

<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;

The registrant's other certifying officer
and I have disclosed, based on our most recent evaluation of internal control
over financial reporting, to the registrant's auditor and the audit committee
of the registrant's board of directors (or persons performing the equivalent
functions);</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>a.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
All significant deficiencies and material
weaknesses in the design or operation of internal control over financial
reporting which are reasonably likely to adversely affect the registrant's
ability to record, process, summarize and report financial information; and</p>



<p style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:1.0in;
margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-.25in'>b.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
Any fraud, whether or not material, that
involves management or other employees who have a significant role in the
registrant's internal control over financial reporting.</p>





<p style='margin:0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt'>Date:&nbsp;
September 7, 2006</p>
